$ VERBAL INFLECTION, not including many grade changes 
	$ preference for these forms: 
		$ participle 
		$ 1sg = 3sg >>> 3pl >> 2sg = 1pl ; generally exclude 2pl as ffit is usually replaced esp in present
		$ 2sg imperative occasionally when most secure
		$ present > aorist >>> past imperfect >> rest 
		$ indic > subj , but in subj 3sg >> 1sg = 3pl >>>>>>> rest 
		$ mediopassive only when diachronically informative
	$ partciple form -- 	
			$ generally aorist stem + -u/onmŐ©, -mŐ©, -nmŐ© 
			$ Source of -onmŐ© ňź -onmŐ© is perhaps from -ontmŐ©, accusative of participle formant -onts, with the -tmŐ© reanalyzed as beng tacked on 
				$ for source of backformation here - {note addition onto 3sg and 3pl inflectional forms of 3sg -ta < -tod 3nsg.nom/acc or -tmŐ©, and 3pl -ta{s} < teŌá{-s}, npl }
				$ alternatively, this is -o-noŐĀm, thematic o + PIE deverbal adjectival suffix -noŐĀm -- cf Sanskrit -ana, Proto-Gmc -anaŐÉ  
					$and cases where it's -nmŐ© are just -noŐĀm 
	$ person-number notes: 
		$ 2pl generally lost in present
		$ 3pl -nt{i} endings often extended to -nta <  -nteŌás , -ntmŐ©? 
		$ 3sg: often become null or just i-mutation; unlike 2sg but like 3sg, feature secondarily grammaticalized elements
			$PAlb -ta {-tmŐ©, teŌá?} in singular often in subjunctive {ket√ę "have.3sg.subj"}, occasoinally indicative presnet {thot√ę "say.3sg" etc.},
			$past.impf -te < -toi? -toŐĄd?  {cf. imperativ3 3sg. -toŐĄd}
			$aor: 3smg distal pronoun may be grammaticalized in as -i; -u after i- final stems
				$ the OAlb forms like suall for sjell for soll-a/i, duall√ę/duall for doll-a/i need an explanation... currently going with -id, consider -swe or -swos or -sos.
	Ő©$ present: often extended with nasal progressive -ne after thematic vowel, often reduced to nj later. 
		$ may be extended in -i-, likely originally derivational
			$ sporadic stem extension in -ot-i- 
		$ 2pl nearly always a secondary formation not datable back to APA let alone PIE ; from -nuŐĄ imperative
		Ő©$ i-mutation in 2sg and 3sg became morphologized by Late Proto-Albanian; ditto for imperative, imperfect, occasional 3sg aorist in -t- 
	$ aorist: 
		$ prefix augment xe- , apply when reasonable
		$ root: lengthened grade in many cases {see Orel 2000}; 
		$ stem suffixes:
			$ sigmatic -es 
			$ -v- endings ; -es + -w- as seen in Latin -ui it seems
				$ cf. Toch -sw-?
			$-t- aorists: decide
			$ -r/n- aorist: just rebracketed final -n from stem
		$ endings: typically secondary, but forms of "BE" are often grammaticalized in before they apply
	$ imperfect: often -es-ne- + BE , but -toŐĄd added to 3sg
	$ mediopassive: from iterative -sceti, but EXTENDED 
		$ for 1SG and 2SG : -sc- + PRIMARY ending + SECONDARY ending + "A" element  {see below} 
			$ "A" : mysterious item reflected as schwa, from o or mŐ© or maybe oi {cf Gk nact -omai?}
				$ or maybe the Ōáe from the acutal Indo-European middle?
		$ e.g. 1sg -sc- + primary -oŌá + secondary -m + A
			$ -x-oŐĄ-m-a > xŇďŐĄma > Old Albanian -hem√ę, -em√ę > -hem, -em, h lost after some consonantal stems
		$ 2sg: -sc- + e-si + s + A > -x…õŐĀs…©sa > -x…õŐĀssa > OAlb {h}esh√ę > {h}esh
			 $single s would disappear if this gemination didn't occur. 
			 	$maybe 3SG is geminated too but we can't tell either way.
		$ 3SG : -sc- + SECONDARY ENDING + the same "A" element
		$ 3sg: -sc- + et + A  > .. > OAlb -het√ę 
		$ 3PL : actually just reflects -sconti with i-mutation? 

		$ 1pl and 2pl : from optative -scoyme and scoyte, with some i-mutating element added at end to make the final -e become -i for both, maybe an -i or-si

		$ PERHAPS all hte endings actuallz come from sc+optatives...
	$iterative -sceti with normal forms grammaticalized in words like 1sg njoh/3sg njeh; shoh/sheh/ etc.

$NOMINAL INFLECTION
	$ per Orel 2000 and it seems others agree, resonant final noun-stems become -o- stems.
	$ plural i-mutation grammaticalized by Late Proto-Albanian
	$ unlike Latin, it seems nominative is often reflected: masc ‚ąÖ < -o-s, neut -eŐą < -a < -mŐ©, -oŐĀm rarely; fem -eŐą < a < aŐĄ < eŌá
	$ pluralizing, perhaps og collective, -eŐąra/-na < -ina per Orel 2000(:229), which causes i-mutation, from a "collectivizing" PIE -iŐĄna he says. I'm treating this as from adjectivalizing -iHn(-os) + collectivizing -eŌá. Since feminine of the latter is listed without accent, ot putting it on, for now. 
	$ MPL i-mutating -eŐąr/-eŐąn treated as from -eŐĀnes, plural of PIE suffix *-eŐĀňźn forming nouns of roots, more in line with De Vaan 2004: 71; Schumacher 2013(:2019) has it via -inih; Orel 2000(: 230) instead has a proposed PIE *-ino for these. 
	$ -nj- mpl form

My proposal, but based on considering the established attribution to *neb į-el-o/a in NIL 500; Hamp 1975ňź 449 apud NIL 503; note also orel 1998(ňź12) for whom it reflects a nŐ©(‚ąÖ)b į-(u)lo "l stem", and Huld 2005(ňź59) for whom it is a compound of nŐ©b įo- and a *wlŐ©Ho. However, this derivation in nŐ©‚ąÖb į-ulos would appear to have regular correspondence to Messapic at-abulus, Latin nebul-a, and Germanic *nebulaz (Old English nifol, Old High German nibul, nebul), and be an unsurprising formal and derivational extension of the well attested stem n(e)bh-o- (Greek neŐĀphos, OCS neŐĀbo, Sanskrit naŐĀbhas). Romanian abure is more consistent with this.

w ňąeňź r t i b į e Ōá , v ňą…Ē …ĺ b …ô , v ňą…Ē …ĺ b …ô $type of clay pot. Attributed to an "early" Slavic loan in wňą…Ďr…™b…Ď by Orel 1998: 514, but this stem does not appear in Derksen 2008, which only has var-i- "to heat (vb.)" and var ä "heat". Demiraj 1997: 424 attributes this and vorbull "whirlpool" to a PIE weŐĄrb{ į}- but this root is unknown. Suffixation in -bh- is possible; applied the general pattern seen in Orel 2000: 151-2 for ibha obha suffixation as also seen in Balto-Slavic. The root, if Demiraj is right on the semantic development, is much more likely {PROPOSAL!} PIE *wert- {e.g. Lat verto} "to turn", with the -t- lost to cluster simplification.
